## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch/reactor rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard observable in chemical kinetics ODE models. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-dependent rate coefficients (e.g., catalyst deactivation or changing conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption in excess-reactant or surface-limited regimes)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; well-mixed batch kinetics)
- Second-order rate law (single-species): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or dimerization proxy)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting when mechanism is unknown)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limitation)
- Generalized autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A) (variable autocatalytic order with finite-capacity limitation)
- Saturating (Monod-like) consumption in A: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by saturation/availability in A)
- Inhibited consumption (self-inhibition): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A) (effective rate decreases at high A due to inhibition/aggregation)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (exponential deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or changing conditions over time)
- Time-accelerating or slowing rate coefficient (power in time): dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A (aging/heating profiles or secular drift in conditions)
- Diffusion/transport-limited apparent rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / sqrt(t + c1) (boundary-layer growth or transport limitation developing in time)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (coexisting unimolecular and bimolecular channels)
- Piecewise-effective rate via smooth switch: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + tanh(c2 * (t - c3))) (activation/deactivation or regime transition in time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stoichiometric consumption typically enforces dA_dt <= 0 for A > 0; sign patterns (negative proportional terms) indicate reactant depletion.
- Linear dependence on A (dA_dt ∝ A) implies exponential-in-time behavior for A(t) under constant conditions; deviations suggest time-varying rates or nonlinearity.
- Higher powers A**c (c > 1) indicate accelerating depletion at high concentration and strong curvature in A(t); commonly associated with bimolecular/chain processes.
- A stable fixed point A = c1 in dA_dt = -c0*(A-c1) signals reversible kinetics or relaxation to equilibrium rather than full depletion to zero.
- Factors of (c - A) indicate finite-capacity limitation or conservation constraints, producing sigmoidal trajectories and an equilibrium/ceiling concentration.
- Rational forms A/(A+c) or A/(c1+c2*A) encode saturation or inhibition: near-zero A gives approximately linear kinetics; large A gives rate plateaus or slowdowns.
- Explicit time factors exp(-c*t) multiplying A represent catalyst activity loss or environmental drift; they produce faster early-time kinetics and slower late-time kinetics than simple first-order.
- Time in denominators like 1/sqrt(t+c) suggests transport limitations developing with time (e.g., diffusion layers), causing progressively slowing apparent reaction rates.
- Sums of terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) indicate parallel reaction pathways; dominance can switch over time as A decreases.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK34)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_f*A**c3
Candidate formulas: 62

GT is the fixed function (independent of \(t\)):
\[
0.7240016388253205\,A^{1/3}-0.1689114325901851\,A^{2}.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) have no effective \(t\)-dependence after parameter choices, and (ii) reduce exactly to a linear combination of \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) with those coefficients (and no extra constant/other \(A\)-powers/Abs artifacts unless they can be removed).

Below, “can match” means there exists a choice of the candidate constants making it identical to GT for all \(A,t\).

---

### 1. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\sin(\cdots(t)\cdots)\)
Set \(c2=0\) to remove the sine term (and all \(t\)-dependence). Then choose \(c0=0.7240016388253205\), \(c1=-0.1689114325901851\). **Can match.**

### 2. \(A^2 c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 + A c3 e^{c4 t} + c5|A|^{c6}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence you’d need \(c1=0\) and \(c4=0\) or the corresponding coefficients zero. But the structure still includes an \(A\) term and a \(|A|^{c6}\) term; you could try to set \(c2=c3=0\) and tune \(|A|^{c6}\) to \(A^{1/3}\), but then you still have \(A^2\) from the first term and \(|A|^{1/3}\) from the last term: that part is plausible only if domain is all real \(A\), because GT uses \(A^{1/3}\) (not \(|A|^{1/3}\)). For all real \(A\), \(A^{1/3}\neq |A|^{1/3}\). So it cannot equal GT on all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 3. \(A^2 c0 + c1|A|^{1/3}\)
Same issue: \(|A|^{1/3}\) cannot equal \(A^{1/3}\) for negative \(A\). If equivalence must hold for all real \(A\), **no match**. (If restricted to \(A\ge 0\), it would match by choosing \(c0=-0.1689\), \(c1=0.7240\), but the task does not state such a restriction.)

### 4. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1\)
Exactly the GT form. Choose \(c0=0.7240016388253205\), \(c1=-0.1689114325901851\). **Can match.**

### 5. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1|A|^2\)
\(|A|^2=A^2\) for all real \(A\). So this is \(c0A^{1/3}+c1A^2\). Choose \(c0=0.7240016388253205\), \(c1=-0.1689114325901851\). **Can match.**

### 6. \(c0|A|^{1/3} + c1|A|^2\)
Again \(|A|^{1/3}\) vs \(A^{1/3}\) prevents equality for negative \(A\). **No match.**

### 7. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3|A|^{c4}\)
You can set \(c1=c2=0\). Then need \(c3|A|^{c4}=0.7240A^{1/3}\), which fails for negative \(A\) because of \(|A|\). **No match.**

### 8. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3\)
Set \(c1=0\). Set \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=0.7240016388253205\), \(c0=-0.1689114325901851\). This gives \(c3A^{1/3}+c0A^2\). **Can match.**

### 9. \(A^2c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\)
Need \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\) issue. **No match.**

### 10. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\)
Set \(c2=0\), then same as candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 11. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\log(Ac3+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches as in candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 12. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A^{c2}c3\)
To match GT exactly, the extra \(A^{c2}\) term must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 13. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\log(c3 e^{c4\sin(Ac5+c6)}+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 14. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{Ac3}\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 15. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2|A|^{c3} + c4\)
Must remove \(Ac1\) and constant: set \(c1=0\), \(c4=0\). Remaining \(|A|^{c3}\) cannot equal \(A^{1/3}\) for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 16. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3 + c4\)
Set \(c1=0\), \(c4=0\), \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=0.7240016388253205\), \(c0=-0.1689114325901851\). **Can match.**

### 17. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + Ac2 + c3\)
Set \(c2=0\), \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 18. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\log(\frac{Ac3}{Ac4+c5}+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 19. \(A^2c0 + A\cdot A^{c1}c2 + Ac3 + A^{c1}c4\)
This contains mixed powers \(A^{c1+1}\), \(A\), and \(A^{c1}\). You could try to set coefficients to zero to leave only \(A^2\) and \(A^{1/3}\), but there is no standalone \(A^{1/3}\) term unless you use \(A^{c1}c4\) with \(c1=1/3\). Then you must kill the \(A^{c1+1}=A^{4/3}\) term by setting \(c2=0\), and kill \(Ac3\) by \(c3=0\). Then you have \(A^2c0 + A^{1/3}c4\), which can match by choosing \(c0=-0.1689\), \(c4=0.7240\). **Can match.**

### 20. \(Ac0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3|A|^{c4}\)
No \(A^2\) term unless you set \(c1=2\) in the \(A^{c1}\) term, but then you still need an \(A^{1/3}\) term; that would have to come from \(|A|^{c4}\) with \(c4=1/3\), which fails for negative \(A\). Alternatively use \(A^{c1}\) for \(1/3\) and \(|A|^{c4}\) for \(2\) (works since \(|A|^2=A^2\)), but then you also have an unavoidable \(A\) term unless \(c0=0\). If \(c0=0\), set \(c1=1/3,c2=0.7240\) and \(c4=2,c3=-0.1689\): then candidate becomes \(0.7240A^{1/3}-0.1689A^2\). That works because \(|A|^2=A^2\). **Can match.**

### 21. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\log(c3 e^{Ac4}+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 22. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{A^{c2}c3}{A^{c2}c4 e^{c5 t}+c6 e^{c5 t}}\)
The fraction equals \(\frac{A^{c2}c3}{e^{c5 t}(A^{c2}c4+c6)} = e^{-c5 t}\cdot \frac{A^{c2}c3}{A^{c2}c4+c6}\).
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c5=0\) or \(c3=0\). Easiest: set \(c3=0\) so the whole fraction vanishes. Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 23. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 24. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{Ac2}{Ac3+c4} + \frac{c5}{Ac3+c4}\)
To avoid rational-in-\(A\) extra terms for all \(A\), set \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 25. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\) (or make sine identically 0, but that’s not possible for all \(t\) via constants). Then you have \(A^2c0+Ac1\), which cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 26. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{c3 t}\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 27. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{c3 t}\log(Ac4+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 28. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence: either \(c2=0\) (kills term) or \(c3=0\) (leaves an \(A\) term). Must set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 29. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A^2 c2 e^{c3 t}\)
Extra \(A^2\) term with \(t\)-dependence; set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 30. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3(A^{c2}+c4)^{c5} + c6\)
To match GT, must remove \(Ac1\) and constant: set \(c1=0\), \(c6=0\). The nonlinear term generally won’t reduce to exactly \(A^{1/3}\) for all \(A\) unless you kill it: set \(c3=0\). Then only \(A^2c0\) remains, missing \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 31. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\)
Set \(c2=0\), \(c4=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 32. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2|A|^{c3} + c4|A|^{c3} + c5\)
Hard to get \(A^{1/3}\) without \(|A|\) issues; also has \(A\) and constant. If you set \(c1=c2=c5=0\), you get \(A^2c0 + c4|A|^{c3}\), still \(|A|^{c3}\) problem for \(1/3\). **No match.**

### 33. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A c2(c3+t)^{c4}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 34. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A\cdot A^{c2}c3 + A^{c2}c4\)
This is \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c3 A^{c2+1} + c4 A^{c2}\).
To avoid extra powers, set \(c3=0\). Then choose \(c2=1/3\) and \(c4=0\) (or \(c4\) absorbed? actually GT already has \(A^{1/3}\) term, but we can just set \(c4=0\)). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 35. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{A c2}{\sqrt{c3+t}}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, must set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 36. \(A c0 + A c1|A|^{c2} + c3|A|^{c4} + c5|A|^{c2}\)
You can get \(A^2\) from \(A c1|A|^{c2}\) by setting \(c2=1\) (gives \(A|A|\), not \(A^2\) for negative \(A\)). Or from \(|A|^{c4}\) with \(c4=2\) (that gives \(A^2\)). But getting \(A^{1/3}\) without \(|A|\) mismatch is not possible. **No match.**

### 37. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 t (A+c3)^{c4}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 38. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\log(c3 t+1)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 39. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{A c2}{A c3 e^{c4 t}+c5 e^{c4 t}}\)
The fraction simplifies to \(\frac{A c2}{e^{c4 t}(A c3+c5)}=e^{-c4 t}\frac{A c2}{A c3+c5}\).
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\) (or \(c4=0\) but then still rational in \(A\)). Setting \(c2=0\) kills it. Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 40. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 t^{c3}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 41. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A^{c2}c3\log(c4 t+1)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 42. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{A c2}{c3 t+c4} + \frac{c5}{c3 t+c4}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), set \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 43. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A^{c2}c3 + c4 t + c5\)
Must remove \(t\) term: set \(c4=0\). Remove constant: set \(c5=0\). Remove extra \(A^{c2}\) term: set \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 44. \(A c0 + c1|A|^{c2} + c3 e^{c4 t}|A|^{c5}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\). Then you have \(A c0 + c1|A|^{c2}\), which cannot produce both \(A^2\) and \(A^{1/3}\) without \(|A|\) mismatch and missing one power. **No match.**

### 45. \(A c0 + c1|A|^{c2} + c3(c4+t)^{c5}|A|^{c6}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\). Then same issue as 44. **No match.**

### 46. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3 e^{c4 t} + c5\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\) (or \(c4=0\) but then extra \(A^{c2}\) remains). With \(c3=0\), you get \(A^2c0+Ac1+c5\). Cannot make \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 47. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{c2 t}{c3 t+c4} + \frac{c5}{c3 t+c4}\)
Extra \(t\)-dependent rational term; to remove it for all \(t\), set \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 48. \(A c0 + A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + c4|A|^{c5}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\) (or \(c3=0\) but then still have \(A^{c1}\)). If \(c2=0\), left with \(A c0 + c4|A|^{c5}\): cannot produce both \(A^2\) and \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 49. \(A^2c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 + c3|A|^{c4}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c1=0\) (or \(c0=0\)). Need no \(A\) term: set \(c2=0\). Then have \(A^2c0 + c3|A|^{c4}\); \(|A|^{c4}\) cannot equal \(A^{1/3}\) for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 50. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 t + c3\)
Set \(c2=0\), \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 51. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + \frac{c2 t}{A c3+c4} + \frac{c5}{A c3+c4}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\). Then remaining rational-in-\(A\) term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 52. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3\sin(c4 t+c5)|A|^{c6}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\). Then \(A^2c0+Ac1+c2\) cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 53. Big rational expression with \((\sqrt A + c1)\) denominators and \(e^{Ac5}\)
To match a polynomial-in-powers \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) for all \(A\), you’d need to eliminate the denominator dependence; no choice of constants makes \((\sqrt A + c1)\) cancel globally without introducing other terms, except setting many numerators to 0 leaving something like \(0\) or \(1/(\sqrt A+c1)\), not GT. **No match.**

### 54. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2\sin(c3 t+c4)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 55. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{c3\sin(c4 t+c5)}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence you can set \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 56. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A^{c2}c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\)
Remove \(t\)-dependence by setting \(c3=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 57. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{Ac3}\cos(c4 t)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), must set \(c2=0\) (since \(\cos(c4 t)\) can’t be constant for all \(t\) unless \(c4=0\), but even then you’d have \(e^{Ac3}\) extra). With \(c2=0\), matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 58. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 e^{c3 t}\log(c4|A|+1)\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
Remove extra term by setting \(c2=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 59. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^2c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t} + c4 e^{c5 t}\)
Set \(c2=0\), \(c4=0\). Then matches candidate 4. **Can match.**

### 60. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3 e^{c4\cos(c5\log(Ac6+1))}\)
Even if you set \(c3=0\) to remove the complicated \(A\)-dependence, you’re left with \(A^2c0+Ac1+c2\) and cannot create \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 61. Rational in \((A+c1)\) with sine(log(|A|))
Hard to reduce to \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) without denominator; setting sine-related coefficients to 0 leaves terms like \(\frac{A^2c0 + A(c2+c3)}{A+c1}\), which is not a sum of \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) for all \(A\). **No match.**

### 62. Similar rational in \((A+c1)\) with log(cos(|A|))
Same denominator obstruction; cannot become \(0.7240A^{1/3}-0.1689A^2\) for all \(A\). **No match.**
